=245  \\$aCorrespondance (concernant la livraison de vin)
=260  \\$aPérigueux; Couze; Bordeaux; Bergerac$c1795-1829
=300  \\$a75 pages
=500  \\$aCorrespondence addressed to Schröder and Schylen, traders in the Chatrons in Bordeaux (and some others),  dated between the year Germinal 3 (march 1795) and 1829. 53 letters signed for the most part by Desmartis and Choiet, traders in Bergerac (2 from Courtois in Perigueux and 1 from Dumare in Couze) The Correspondence concerns the delivery of wine. 51 postmarks from Bergerac and 2 from Perigueux. (info Antiquarian)
=500  \\$aThe Bergerac & Périgord (Courtois & Couze) were wine-growing regions, a subregion of South West France,  which corresponds roughly to the current  Dordogne Department. Bordeaux, hub of the famed wine-growing region, is a port city on the Garonne River in southwestern France.

=100  \\$aMengozzi, Bernardo$d1758-1800$4edt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q19998065$98165
=245  \\$aMéthode de chant du Conservatoire de Musique
=260  \\$aParis$bConservatoire de musique$c1803-4
=300  \\$a[vii]-290-[2] pages
=500  \\$aLargely the work of Bernardo Mengozzi, a member of the commission for preparing the Méthod de chant (cf. Avertissement)
=500  \\$aContains many musical examples by various composers, ranging in length from a few measures of recitative to complete solfèges and arias in vocal score.
The recitatives are by Sacchini (p. 68), Glu[c]k (p. 68-69), and Piccinni (p. 69-70).
The solfèges are by P.P. Colonna (p. 86-87), Bononcini (p. 88-89), Benedetto Marcello (p. 90-91), Hasse (p. 92-94), Galuppi (p. 95-97), Porpora (p. 98-99), A. Scarlatti (p. 100-01), Caffaro [i.e. Cafaro] (p. 102-105), L. Vinci (p. 106-107), L. Leo (p. 108-109), Traetta (p. 110-113), N. Conforto (p. 114-115), D. Alberti (p. 116-117), Jom[m]elli (p. 118-123), Gasparini (p. 124-125), G. Latilla (p. 126-128), Piccinni (p. 129-132), Pergolese (p. 132-133), Manna (p. 134-135), N. Sala (p. 136-138), F. Maio [i.e. Gian Francesco Majo?] (p. 138-143), Costanzi (p. 144-145), Terradellas (p. 146-148), Perez (p. 148-50), M. Vento (p. 150-153), Cimarosa (p. 154-159), G.C. [i.e. Johann Christian] Bach (p. 159-162; this is "Chiari fonti" from the Bach/Guglielmi arrangement of Gluck's Orfeo, without its orchestral introduction and coda; Terry p. 234, no. 2), Sacchini (p. 162-165), Anfossi (p. 165-168), and Sarti (p. 168-172).
The "Choix d'airs de différens caractères" are by Hasse (p. 174-178), L. Leo (p. 178-179 and 188-191), A. Hasse (p. 180-182), Jom[m]elli (p. 182-187, 220-227, 228-232, 236-241, and 254-257), P. Caffaro [i.e. Cafaro] (p. 192-195), N. Piccinni (p. 195-199 and 208-212), A. Sacchini (p. 200-203, 213-219, 232-235, and 268-273), G. [i.e. Johann Christian] Bach (p. 204-207; "La sorte mia spietata," Terry, p. 251, no. 4 (mistranscribed)), S. Sarti (p. 242-247), D. Cimarosa (p. 248-253 and 286-290), J. Maio [i.e. Gian Fancesco Majo or Giuseppe de Majo] (p. 258-263 and 280-285), B. Galuppi (p. 264-267), and T. Traetta (p. 274-279).

=245  \\$aChoralbuch zu dem neuen Bremischen Gesangbuch, betitelt Christliches Gesangbuch zur Befördeung öffentlicher und häuslicher Andacht.
=260  \\$aRinteln$bSteuber$c1821
=300  \\$aiv-92 pages$bleather bound, gilded edges$coblong
=500  \\$aJ.H. Lange was organist, singer (tenor), conductor and composer.
=500  \\$aHe was the son of the teacher and organist at St Stephen's in Bremen Johann Lange ( 1755-1815), had his musical training with Peter Winter in Munich, and returned to Bremen in 1804, initially as his father's assistant, before taking over his father's position as organist at St Stephen's in 1809. Lange played first violin in the orchestra of the Privat-Concerte and performed in concerts (especially at the Sing-Akademie) as a tenor. He was also founding member of the Singschule, the Sing-Akademie (later an honorary member) and, in 1827, of the Liedertafel (temporarily its conductor).

=245  \\$a[Picture book Grietje Dekker, 1852]$bA collection of hand colored engravings of various subjects: the months, ships, occupations
=260  \\$aAugsburg$bs.n.$c1799-1852
=300  \\$a15 pages$boblong booklet with engraved illustrations, hand colored with watercolor 
=500  \\$aConsist of several collections:
- page 1-3: The months of the year. Four images on each page with scenes depicting a scene from that time of year, and a little vignet with the astrological sign in the top corner. Engravings by Johann Sebastian Muller (from Nuremberg), published by Schmidhammer, 'No. 101' at the bottom of the first page. 
- page 4-7: ships and people on boats. Published by Martin Engelbrecht in Augsburg with royal privilege (C.P. Maj = Cum Privilegio Majestatis), No. 367, dated 1849, 1850, 1851, 1852.
- page 8-11: Four pages with rows of figures in 18th c. costumes with various occupations, related to hunting, various ones with musical instruments, ladies in gowns,  men on horseback. Published by Schmidhammer in Nuremberg, Nr. 130.
- page 12-15: 'Le Douze Mois / Die 12 Monath': rows of small scenes depicting the twelve months of the year, starting in december. Published by Engelbrecht in Augsburg, Nr. 357, with royal privilege (C.P. Maj.), dated 1799, 1800, 1801, 1802.
=500  \\$aJohann Sebastian Müller was a botanist and engraver from Nuremberg. He signed his works as J.S. Müller until 1760, after that date he went by 'John Miller', as he had moved to London.   
=500  \\$aBoth Johann Christoph Schmidhammer and Martin Engelbrecht were known for publishing prints. They were not necessarily the artists themselves, though in some cases they are. 
=500  \\$aAll pictures in this collection depict old-fashioned scenes and costumes. The collection is from 1852 but the images all look destinctly 18th c.

=500  \\$aLa Dame Blanche is an opera by François-Adrien Boieldieu,  on a libretto by Eugene Scribe, premiere Opéra Comique Paris 1825

=500  \\$aIn the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.
=501  \\$aContains, besides the essay and a lithograph, an extract from the libretto of Boieldieu's 'La Dame Blanche' (Apollon en Helvétie : Chœur de table), and 'Der Freune Tonlied'

=500  \\$aWillem Karel Hendrik Friso (1711-1751) was the first 'Erfstadhouder' of the United Provinces
=500  \\$ahe married Anne, Princess Royal, on 25 March 1734
=500  \\$aPrincess Anne (in Dutch also known as Anna van Hannover) had been a pupil of Georg Friedrich Händel. 
Händel did not like teaching, but said he would "make the only exception for Anne, flower of princesses" 
The music played at her wedding, This is the day was set by Handel to the princess's own words based on Psalms 45 and 118. Handel also composed an operatic entertainment, Parnasso in Festa, in honour of her wedding which was performed for the first time at the King's Theatre, London, on 13 March 1734, with great success.

=100  \\$aHaydn, Joseph$d1732-1809$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7349$94783
=245  \\$aA Select Collection of Original Scottish Airs for the Voice$nVol. 3
=246  \1$aFifty Scottish Songs, with Symphonies & Acccompaniments, $bWholly by Haydn, Vol. III
=250  \\$a1st ed. 
=260  \\$aLondon$aEdinburg$bPreston$bThomson$c1802
=300  \\$a[i]-4-[ii]-100 pages$balternating pages of text and music, Vol. 3 and Vol. 4 bound together, contains a full page portrait of Robert Burns
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 6 vols., 1793-1841
=500  \\$a"A Select Collection of Original Scottish Airs for the Voice" is a multi-volume collection of Scottish song edited and published by the entrepreneurial musician, publisher and Clerk to the Board of Trustees for Encouragement of Art and Manufacture in Scotland, George Thomson. For the first volume, which appeared in 1793, Thomson commissioned the composer Ignaz Pleyel to provide musical settings.[wikipedia]

From the Preface of this Vol. 3: "For the composition of these [the symphonies and accompaniments], he entered into terms with Mr Pleyel, who fulfilled part of his engagement very satisfactorily; but having then deserted it, the Editor, after a fruitless correspondence with him, which retarded the progress of the Work for years, at length found it necessary to turn his eyes elsewhere. He was so fortunate, however, [...] as to engage Mr Kozeluch and Dr Haydn, to proceed with the Work, which they have finished in such a manner, as to leave him without any other regret, but that of having so long delayed his application to them." 
=500  \\$aContains a portrait of Robert Burns (bound between Vol. 3 and 4) by A. Nasmyth and Paton Thomson. 
=500  \\$aContains a full page engraved illustration "The Soldier's Return", which seems to belong to a song from Vol. 1.
=501  \\$aBound in with Vol. 4 of the same collection.
=590  \\$aWith Introductory & Concluding Symphonies & Accompaniments for the Piano Forte, Violin & Violoncello by Pleyel, Kozeluch & Haydn. With Select & Characteristic Verses both Scottish and English adapted to the Airs, including upwards of One Hundred New Songs by Burns.

=500  \\$aBookseller's slip: "In-8 e xvi, 348,& [1] non ch., relié plein veau blond, dos à nerfs orné (rel d'époque). Fils d'un peintre de renom, c'est le seul écrit de cet acteur fortuné qui fit carrière en Allemagne, en Belgique (où il fut directeur du Théâtre de la Monnaie), et en France. Rédigé à l'usage des prétendants acteurs et actrices, il contient de nombreux détails sur la vie des troupes, le jeu d'acteur et le status de comédien. Statut fort peu en odeur de sainteté, l'église excommuniant alors la profession. D'Hannetaire « en vertu d'un ancien usage de la comédie » renonça en 1768 par-devant notaire au status, mais pas à la pratique. Légères épidermures sans gravité, infime rousseur encadrant le titre, bon exemplaire."

=500  \\$aAbraham Hosemann (1561-1617), an imperial historiographer, was a man who, although Henelius rightly called him omnium bipedum mendacissimum, nevertheless had some influence on Silesian provincial and local historiography in earlier times.
=590  \\$aAbgebildet an dem unverendertem Vorsatz des frommen Patriarchen Jacobs, als er bey schwerem Dienste, seine ihm versprochene, hertzgewüntschte Jungfraw Rahel, nicht allein vierzehen gantzer Jahr vor dem Ehelichen Beylager, sondern auch bestendiglichen geliebet und lieb gehalten, biß in den Todt, und nach dem Tode: oder die wunderschöne Historia und denckwürdige Geschicht, der Heyrat Jacobs, im ersten Buch Mosis am 29. Capittel. Zu sonderbarem unvergessenem Ruhm, und stetwehrendem Gedächtnüß auch hochnützlichen Erinnerungen, denen Ehrenvesten, Wolbenambten, Erbarn und vorsichtigen jungen Gesellen, allen und jeden, Bürgers Söhnen, und Zuchtliebenden Jünglingen, so wol allen und jeden, züchtigen, Edlen, viel Ehrentugentreichen Jungfrawen, Bürgers Töchtern, hoch und nider Standes Personen, in der Uhralten, mächtigen, und Edlen Provinz, des Christlichen Landes Preussen, sonderlich der drey See-Haupt- und Handelsstädte, Dantzig, Thoren, und Margenberg, in gebührender Unterthänigkeit, mit erzehlung der aller denckwürdigsten, und lustigsten Historien, dedicirt: durch Abrahamum Hossmannum, Laubanensum Lusatium, Sacr. Cæsar. Majestat. Historicum.

=041  \\$alat$heng
=100  \\$aBacon, Francis$d1561-1626$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q37388$94892
=240  \\$aThe Advancement of Learning
=245  \\$aDe augmentis scientiarum lib. IX
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bRavelstein$c1662
=300  \\$a[xx]-607-[67] pages$bleather bound,  engraved fronispiece, rigid binding
=500  \\$aOriginally 'Of Proficience and Advancement of Learning Divine and Human' was published in 1605, and is written in the form of a letter to King James.
=500  \\$a Francis Bacon was an English philosopher, statesman, scientist, lawyer, jurist, author, and pioneer of the scientific method. Although his political career ended in disgrace, he remained extremely influential through his works, especially as philosophical advocate and practitioner of the scientific method during the scientific revolution.

=500  \\$aBacon has been called the creator of empiricism. His works established and popularized inductive methodologies for scientific inquiry, often called the Baconian method, or simply the Scientific Method. His demand for a planned procedure of investigating all things natural marked a new turn in the rhetorical and theoretical framework for science, much of which still surrounds conceptions of proper methodology today.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aLa Roche-Guilhem, Anne de$d1644-1707$4aut$98371
=245  \\$aNouvelles historiques
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bBulderen, van$c1691
=300  \\$a128 pages
=500  \\$aAnne de La Roche-Guilhem was a Huguenot emigré, a French writer and translator. Ex libris Ignác Karel, Count of Sternberg, ?-1700, who among others was Geheimrat and Kammerherr to the Emperor, and who had contacts with the Irish fraternity in Prague
=505  \\$gPremière partie: 'Gaston Phebus, Comte de Foix' -- Seconde partie: 'La Prédiction accomplie' -- troisième partie: 'Les deux fortunes imprévues'
=520  \\$aThe daughter of Charles de Guilhen and Marie-Anne d'Azemar, she was, by her mother, a grand-niece of the poet Antoine Girard de Saint-Amant. Anne de La Roche-Guilhem became known by several works of fiction. A Protestant, she emigrated to England on the revocation of the Edict of Nantes (1685), perhaps via the Netherlands. Her father having died without a fortune, and she herself having never abjured from Protestantism, she sought in vain for protectors by dedicating some of her works to princesses, or to Charles II. Rare in all, her comedy-ballet, was composed for the King's birthday (1677). She also translated Spanish works. Finally, settled in London, she died there surrounded by Huguenot friends. The circulation of her works written in England, printed in Holland, secretly distributed in France, shows how the Protestant networks worked in this troubled time. 
=561  \\$aEx libris Passe Historico (manuscript), Bibliotheca Ill.mi ecc. Exccell: D.D. Ignatij Caroli S: R: Imp. Comitis de Sternberg (manuscript), Bibliotheca P.P. Hibernorum ad Ambrosium Prague Sub lit. G. 12° 370 (manuscript); Former shelf marks L.41 (pencil) and H.XI.282 (ink)

=100  \\$aLackington, James$d1746-1815$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q6137696$98413
=245  \\$aMemoirs of the Forty-Five First Years of the Life of James Lackington, Bookseller
=250  \\$a10th ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bLackington$c1795
=300  \\$a328 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aJames Lackington (1746-1815) was a bookseller who is credited with revolutionizing the British book trade.  He is best known for refusing credit at his shop which allowed him to reduce the price of books throughout his store. He printed catalogues of his stock; according to Lackington's biography, the first edition contained 12,000 titles. He bought whole libraries and published writers' manuscripts. He also saved remaindered books from destruction and resold them at bargain prices, firmly believing that books were the key to knowledge, reason and happiness and that everyone, no matter their economic background, social class or gender, had the right to access books at cheap prices. (source: wiki)

=041  \\$aita
=100  \\$aGuarini, Battista$d1538-1612$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q542039$95920
=245  \\$aIl Pastor Fido$bTragicomedia Pastorale
=260  \\$aRome$bHercole$cs.d.
=300  \\$a243 pages$bbound in white velum, engraved title page, illustrations, manuscript notes on frontpapers
=500  \\$aa beautifully illustrated duodecimo, anonymous full page illustrations at the start of the prologue and each of the 5 acts 
=500  \\$aliterature suggests a publication-date ca. 1640
=500  \\$aIl pastor fido is a tragicomedy by Battista Guarini in five acts or 6862 verses. It was written between 1580 and 1584 and first published as a book in Venice in 1590. The first performance may have taken place in 1593 in Siena; the first historically verified performance in 1595 in Crema. Guarini continued to revise the play after the first publication, the last revision being for the 20th edition of 1602 (Venice). It appeared in over a hundred editions following its first publication. 
=500  \\$aIn Italian literature, Il pastor fido, among others, marks the transition from Italian Renaissance to Baroque theatre. 
=500  \\$aTogether with Bonarelli's 'Filli di Sciro' and Tasso's 'Aminta', Guarini's 'Il pastor fido' is considered one of the masterpieces of the genre of the pastoral drama 
=500  \\$aOne of the most famous plays of the 17th century, it inspired numerous madrigal composers, including Giaches de Wert, Claudio Monteverdi, Sigismondo d'India, Alessandro Grandi, Tarquinio Merula, and Heinrich Schütz; Philippe de Monte named a volume after the play. The first operatic treatment was Handel's HWV 8 in 1712.
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Rime' and Tasso's 'Aminta'
=561  \\$aEx libris  illegible  (manuscript)
=590  \\$aOra in questa nuova impressione di belissime Figure in Rame ornato Con licenza de Superiore

=500  \\$aAminta was written by in 1573, represented during a garden party at the court of Ferrara. Both the actors and the public were noble persons living at the Court, who could understand subtle allusions the poet made to that style of life, in contrast with the life of shepherds, represented in an idyllic way. 
=500  \\$aFirst published in 1580
=500  \\$aTogether with Guarini's 'Il pastor fido' and Bonarelli's 'Filli di Sciro', Tasso's 'Aminta' is considered one of the masterpieces of the genre of the pastoral drama
=501  \\$aBound in with Guarini's 'Il pastor fido' and 'Rime' 
=561  \\$aEx libris illegible (manuscript)

=500  \\$aMarie Pélissier (1706-1749) was a French operatic soprano. At the Paris Opera in 1722, she began her career, which was noted for her artistic skill and a scandal, until her retirement in 1741. A scandal involving the theft of gold and money from the Jewish financier François Lopez Dulis, led to Pélissier's dismissal on February 15, 1734, whereupon she fled to London. She was back at the Paris Opera on April 19, 1735, remaining there until retiring in October 1741.

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAmbrosius Lobwasser (1515–1585) was a German humanist and translator, born in Saxony. He is best known for his Psalter des Königlichen Propheten David, published in 1573 (Leipzig). This metrical psalter, a translation of the Genevan Psalter, became one of the standard psalm-books used by the evangelical churches of the German-speaking lands, including Switzerland (the Genevan Psalter had been written in French). The Lobwasser psalter was widely reprinted into the 1800s.

=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bMunster$c1864
=300  \\$a16 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aTribute poem in memory of Joost van den Vondel, performed on the stage of the Amsterdam Stadschouwburg in 1818, after the performance of Vondel's play "Gysbrecht van Aemstel" (see 03H05). The play was written to inaugurate Amsterdam's first city theatre on 3 January 1638, and was then performed annually (on New Year's Day) in Amsterdam until 1968.

=100  \\$aFigliucci, Felice$dc. 1524-c. 1590$4trl$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3742149$98465
=245  \\$aCatechismo cioè Istruttione secondo il Decreto del Concilio di Trento a' Parochi
=260  \\$aVenice$bAngelieri$c1605
=300  \\$a[xv]-578-[20] pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aCatechism of the Catholic Counter-Reformation with the norms and conclusions laid down by the Council of Trent (closed in 1563) in response to the Lutheran Reformation.
=500  \\$aPope Pius IV entrusted the composition of the Catechism to four distinguished theologians: Leonardo Marini, Archbishop of Lanciano; Muzio Calini, Archbishop of Zara; Egidio Foscherari, Bishop of Modena; and Francisco Foreiro, a Portuguese Dominican.
Three cardinals were appointed to supervise the work. Charles Borromeo superintended the redaction of the original Italian text, which was finished in 1564. Cardinal William Sirletus then gave it the final touches, and the famous Humanists, Julius Pogianus and Paulus Manutius, translated it into classical Latin.
=500  \\$aFelice Figliucci (Felix Filliucius, cloister name Alexus) (c. 1525 – c. 1590), an Italian humanist, philosopher, and theologian translated the Latin Catechism back into Italian in 1567 at the order of the Pope. 
=534  \\$cCatechismus ex decreto Concilii Tridentini ad parochos Pii V jussu editus, Romae (Rome: Manuzio, 1566)

=041  \\$aita
=245  \\$aDue tragedie: La Merope e la Demodice
=260  \\$aLondon$bTonson$c1721
=300  \\$a226 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aGiovanni Battista Recanati (1687-1734 or 1735) was a Venetian writer, poet and playwright, also known by the pseudonym of Teleste Ciparissiano. He was a collaborator of the «Giornale dei Letterati d'Italia», member of the Academy of Arcadia and of that of Crusca from 1727. Besides promoting literary initiatives, he was a bibliophile and book collector.
=500  \\$aFrancesco Scipione Maffei (1675-1755) was a Venetian writer and art critic, author of many articles and plays. Maffei was of the illustrious family that originated in Bologna. He studied for five years in Parma, at the Jesuit College, and afterwards, from 1698, at Rome, where he became a member of the Accademia degli Arcadi. He then founded an "Arcadian Academy" in his hometown Verona. In 1709, he went to Padua, where he briefly collaborated with Apostolo Zeno and Antonio Valisnieri in editing the ambitious literary periodical the Giornale de' Letterati d'Italia, which had but a short career. Subsequently, an acquaintance with the actor Riccoboni led him to exert himself for the improvement of dramatic art in Italy and a revitalized Italian theatre.
=500  \\$aScipione Maffei premiered his tragedy Merope in Verona on June 12, 1713; it quickly became popular throughout Italy and beyond. By agreement with Maffei, Voltaire went on to adapt the play, which was eventually staged in 1743 as Mérope.
=500  \\$aMerope was a Queen of Messenia in Greek mythology, daughter of King Cypselus of Arcadia and wife of Cresphontes, the Heraclid king of Messenia. After the murder of her husband and her two older children by Polyphontes (another Heraclid), Merope was forced to marry the murderer, but she managed to save her youngest son Aepytus, whom she sent secretly to Aetolia. Several years later, when Aepytus grew up, he killed Polyphontes with the collaboration of Merope, and he took revenge for the murder of his relatives and the insult to his mother.
=561  \\$aEx libris Livraria Castro 'Olisipo; se queres vencer des perta e luta' (plate of a rare book store in Lisbon)
Ex libris L. d'Almd. d'Albuquerque (ms. on frontispiece)

=246  \1$aA new and true report, in which we give an account of the happy success that had a squadron of five Dutch warships, which were in charge of General Duardo Esprago Cavalleiro Ollandez, defeating & burning seven ships of Turks, within the port of Buxia
=260  \\$aMalta$bs.n.$c1673
=300  \\$a7 pages
=500  \\$aSir Edward Spragge or Spragg, whose name is Frenchified as Edward Sprague (1629-1673), was an admiral in the Royal Navy. Sprague was an Irish officer who fought for England after the restoration of King Charles II. In 1670 and 1671 Spragge fought the Barbary pirates on the Revenge (a warship).
=500  \\$aThe Barbary Corsairs or Pirates operated out of the principal Mediterranean ports of North Africa - Tripoli, Tunis and Algiers - terrorising all shipping in the region and mounting raids against coastal settlement throughout Europe in search of slaves. In the spring of 1671, Edward Spragge sailed with a fleet to Bougie Bay ("Buxia" or Béjaïa (https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Béjaïa)), near Algiers, where on 8 May, after a sharp fight, he burnt and destroyed ten corsair ships.
=500  \\$aRare pamphlet, which was originally published in Spanish reporting a letter by Edward Spragge to the consul of the English nation in Granada. Printed by Pedro Castera as 'Nueva relacion y traslado de una carta escrita por el excelentissimo señor don Eduardo Espragg, general de la armada del serenissimo rey de Inglaterra, y de la Gran Bretaña, a don Onofre Colston, consul de la nacion inglesa en el reyno de Granada, y residente en la ciudad de Malaga, &c., donde se le da cuenta de la feliz victoria, y destrozo que ha hecho en los Turcos, en el Puerto de Buxia, navios que echo a pique, capitanes, y moros que murieron' (Malaga, 1671) (https://iberian.ucd.ie/view/iberian:129216)

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aDe snaaksche Clement Marot op zyn praatstoel verhalende over de driehondert koddige historien en snaakeryen
=260  \\$aCologne$bGaillard
=300  \\$a[ii]-320 pages$b5 plates & 1 folded sheet inserted
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aCollection of anecdotes, as if from the mouth of the witty and most shrewd among the court jesters Clement Marot, that was published in the middle of the eighteenth century, probably in Amsterdam. The imprint Jacobus Gaillard in Cologne is a fictitious printer's address.
=500  \\$aClement Marot (1496 – 1544) is known, among other things, for his Psalm rhyming of 1541. He was also the court poet to King Francis I. Shortly after his death, all kinds of existing jokes, farces and anecdotes were written to his name, as was the case with his compatriots François Villon and Rabelais. In the Netherlands it was the poet, innkeeper and actor Jan Zoet who published a collection of anecdotes (translated or not, unknown) in 1655 under the title 'Het leven en bedrijf van Clement Marot', a collection that has been reprinted far into the nineteenth century. However 'De snaaksche Clement Marot' only has Marot's name in common with that work.
=500  \\$acontains an excessively rare inserted fold-out leaf before page 148, illustrating the anecdote "De Kluchtige ontdekking"

=100  \\$aLa Harpe, Jean-François de$d1739-1803$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q379022$98415
=245  \\$aCorrespondance littéraire, adressée à son Altesse Impériale Mr. Le Grand-Duc aujourd'hui Empereur de Russie et à M. le Comte André Schowalow, chambellan de l'Impératrice Catherine II$nvols. 1-6
=260  \\$aParis$bMigneret$c1804-07
=300  \\$a6 vols. (xxiv-423+[iv]-424+[iv]-400+[iv]-334+[iv]-404+[iv]-218-4 pages)
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aJean-François de La Harpe (1739-1803) was a French playwright, writer and literary critic. He took part in the quarrel between the Gluckists and the Piccinists, an aesthetic controversy that divided the Parisian musical world between 1775 and 1779, where the defenders of French opera (Gluckists) and the supporters of Italian music (Piccinists) were opposing each other. La Harpe was, together with Marmontel and d'Alembert, a proponent of Italian music.
=500  \\$aLa Harpe's Literary Correspondence, addressed to the Grand Duke Paul of Russia, is full of theatrical anecdotes about the actors and plays of his time. 
=500  \\$aCorrespondence held between 1774 and 1789

=041  \\$aeng
=100  \\$aChurchill, Charles$d1732-1764$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1063958$98487
=245  \\$aPoems
=260  \\$aDublin$bWilson$c1764
=300  \\$a2 vols. ([vi]-184+[vi]-179 pages) $bengraved frontispiece
=500  \\$aCharles Churchill (1732-1764) was a poet and satirist
=500  \\$aVol. 1 contains an engraved portrait (anonymous) of the author; vol. 2 contains a portrait engraving (Byrne after Miller) of John Wilkes (1725-1797). After 1761 or 1762 Churchill became a close ally and friend with Wilkes, the champion of liberty of the press, a British radical journalist and politician, as well as a magistrate, essayist and soldier. 
=500  \\$aChurchill's knowledge of the theatre prevails in the 'Rosciad', which appeared in March 1761. This reckless and amusing satire describes with the most disconcerting accuracy the faults of the various actors and actresses on the London stage; in a competition judged by Shakespeare and Jonson, Garrick is named the greatest English actor. 'The Duellist' (1763) is a virulent satire on the most active opponents of Wilkes in the House of Lords; The 'Epistle to William Hogarth' (1763) was in answer to the caricature of Wilkes made during the trial, in it Hogarth's vanity and envy were attacked in an invective which Garrick quoted as shocking and barbarous; 'In Night, an Epistle to Robert Lloyd' (1761), Churchill answered the attacks made on him, offering by way of defense the argument that any faults were better than hypocrisy; 'The Prophecy of Famine: A Scots Pastoral' (1763) is founded on a paper written originally for The North Briton. It is a violent satire on Scottish influence.
=505  \\$gThe Rociad -- The Apology -- Night -- The Prophecy of famine -- Epistle to William Hogarth -- The Ghost -- The Conference - The Author -- The Duellist -

=100  \\$aHagedorn, Friedrich von$d1708-1754$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q63985$96793
=245  \\$aDes herrn Friedrichs von Hagedorn sämmtliche poetische Werke$nvols. 1-3
=260  \\$aHamburg$bBohn$c1771
=300  \\$a3 vols. in 1 (xxviii-130-[2]+178-[10]+xxii-180-[2] pages)$bfrontispiece engraving, engraved title page
=500  \\$aHagedorn incorporated ancient, French and above all English inspirations into cheerful, sensible fables and tales (1738) and anacreontic, dallying odes and songs (1742-1752). Formally, his works can be divided into fables, songs, didactic poems and epigrams. His poetry is kept simple (alternating verse, easily singable stanzaic forms) and pursues different stylistic ideals than the poets of the Baroque. 
=500  \\$aMozart set his poem Die Alte (The Old Woman) in his song of the same name (K. 517) in 1787. Joseph Haydn set two of his poems in his canons (a capella songs) (Hob. XXVIIb). 
=500  \\$aFrontipiece portrait of Hagedorn engraved by J.C.G.Fritsch after van der Schmissen
=505  \\$gvol. 1: Moralische Gedichte - Epigrammatische Gedichte$gvol. 2: Fabel und Erzählungen$gvol. 3: Oden und Lieder - Abhandlungen von den Liedern der alten Griechen

=100  \\$aÅhlström, Olof$d1756-1835$4cmp$4edt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q327530$98488
=245  \\$aSkalde-stycken satte i musik$nvols. 7-8

=300  \\$a2 vols. (47-35+48-36 pages)
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$a2 vols. in 1; both having a textual and a musical part, with the music printed on thicker paper
=500  \\$aOlof Åhlström (1756-1835) was an organist and composer. His own compositions include a large number of songs, among them many poems by Anna Maria Lenngren, who was his sister-in-law, that he had set to music. These were published in several parts of Skalde-stycken satte i musik (1794–1823). He also composed a number of chorales, a cantata, fourteen sonatas, and an opera, Frigga (1787).

=245  \\$aHistoire de Madame De Luz;  anecdotte du règne d'Henri IV
=260  \\$aThe Hague$bHondt, de$c1741

=500  \\$aThrough a vivid portrait of a woman of sovereign innocence, Duclos denounces the hypocrisy of a prudish society. Madame de Luz is a sort of libertine Princess of Cleves, a moralist's novel that is also a praise of femininity.
=504  \\$aMadame de Luz is one of the most beautiful women in the kingdom of Henry IV, virtuous and loyal to her husband. She is secretly in love with the Marquis de Saint-Geran, but tries to forget this passion.

Her husband, the Baron de Luz, is involved in a plot led by the Maréchal de Biron, Governor of Burgundy, to overthrow Henry IV. Arrested, the Baron de Luz is threatened with the death penalty. Convinced of his innocence and determined to free him, Madame de Luz intervenes with one of the judges at the trial, Monsieur de Thurin, a suitor whom she had once spurned. Thurin is ready to clear the Baron's name if she accepts his advances. Madame de Luz resists and then gives in to the blackmail. Her life then turns upside down. She has committed a sin from which she will never recover.

=300  \\$a[ii]- XXVII-56-[12]-189 pages$bfolded page with engraved plate
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aFirst edition of this curious and unusual work, in which the author, physician to the polish King Stanislas (Stanisław I Leszczyński 1677-1766) seeks to study the "influence of the passions" on the development of diseases: this is one of the first treatises on the subject, which was very popular at the end of the 18th and beginning of the 19th centuries. The author deals in particular with the effects of music and analyses the way in which singing and instruments can act on the passions

=100  \\$4aut$aMeerten-Schilperoort, Anna Barbara van$d1778-1853$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2138933$923916
=245  \\$aAlmanak voor de jeugd voor 1830
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bBeijerinck$c1830
=300  \\$a[x]-110-[2] pages$billustrations some of them coloured, engraved title page
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAlmanak voor de Jeugd was published 1827 - 1839, Amsterdam, by  G.J.A. Beijerinck. 
=500  \\$aThe Almanak voor de Jeugd contained an annual year calendar with religious holidays, and consists mainly of moralising stories and poems specially written for children
=500  \\$aAnna Barbara Van Meerten-Schilperoort, writer, educator and school teacher, is herself responsible for all the stories and the play and will continue to do so over twenty years. For the little poems, which she loves but does not write herself, she is dependent on the input of others. 
=500  \\$aVan Meerten-Schilperoort published several books on education, advice to women, novels, and other works. In 1821–1835, she was the editor of the paper Penelope. Her school became one of the most notable institutes of education for women in the Netherlands. She spoke for difference feminism, and argued that women should be given a more public role in the service of the state. In 1832 she started philanthropic work for the betterment of the conditions of female prisoners, and in 1841, she founded the charity association Hulpbetoon aan Eerlijke en Vlijtige Armoede, which was the first women's organization in the Netherlands. She has been referred to as the founder of the organized women's rights movement in the Netherlands.

=100  \\$aChapelle, Claude Emmanuel Luillier$d1626-1686$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1096324$98503
=100  \\$aBauchaumont, François Le Coigneaux de$d1624-1702$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3085110$98504
=100  \\$aLefèbvre de Saint-Marc, Charles Hugues$d1698-1769$4win$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2421209$98505
=245  \\$aŒuvres de Chapelle et de Bachaumont
=260  \\$aThe Hague; Paris$bQuillau$c1755
=300  \\$alxxvi-320 pages$btitle page in red and black ink
=500  \\$aChapelle was a French man of letters of the Grand Siècle, who has been remembered in literary history for having been a close friend of three major authors of the time: Cyrano de Bergerac, D'Assoucy and Molière, and for having written, with François Le Coigneux de Bachaumont, a Voyage in prose and verse which was the model for many other stories in the same form. He was also close to François Bernier, La Fontaine, Racine, Boileau and Chaulieu, and his lightness of spirit and playfulness earned him, towards the end of his life, a place in the Parisian salons and the appreciation of several of the "grand seigneurs" of the court of Louis XIV.
=500  \\$aBachaumont was a french poet .A friend of Chapelle, he made with him the gai Voyage en Provence et en Languedoc (Sept. 1656), stopping at the castle of Blois, at the home of Gaston d'Orléans himself, then heading for Guyenne where they met the count of Jonzac at Blaye, Agen where they met the marquis of Saint-Luc, at Graulhet at the home of the count of Aubijoux, at the castle of Pennautier, near Carcassonne, at the home of the Treasurer of the States, Reich de Pennautier, at Encausse at the home of the Marquis de Fontrailles, seneschal of Armagnac, and whose relation, which is one of the first models of this pleasant and easy poetry, dictated by pleasure and indolence, has immortalised them both.
=500  \\$aSaint Marc was a french playwright, known in the republic of letters by works of various genres, and especially by editions of various authors

=100  \\$aPène du Bois, Henri$d1858-1906$4aut$98506
=245  \\$aFour Private Libraries of New York: A Contribution to the History of Bibliophilism in America
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aNew York$bDuprat$c1892
=300  \\$a119 pages$bunpaginated pages with illustrations (engravings, photos, litographs), title page in red and black ink, coloured and black&white llithographs preceded by a tissue, front and back matter consists of each 10 blanco pages
=500  \\$aHenri Pène du Bois, an American writer, literary critic, and journalist whose friendship with French author Guy de Maupassant (1850-1893) was the source of his son’s name. Born in a cultured, sophisticated family of French origin but with roots in America dating back to 1748, he was an avowed francophile and created a sophisticated environment deeply engaged in the French culture. He accompanied his son Guy, a painter, on a trip to Paris in 1905. His tragic death in 1906 on board of the ship for their return home to America forced Guy to turn to art criticism to help support his family.

=500  \\$a"Mr L'Abbé de Villiers, si connu par son Art de prêcher, & par plusieurs autres Ouvrages, qui ont eu l'aprobation du public" (in Oeuvres de Monsieur de Saint Evremond, I,  p.296)
=500  \\$aDe Villiers wrote many works in the seventeenth century, and many biographies and studies are attributed to him, such as Lettres sur l'oraison des quiétistes or Prière en vers sur l'espérance qu'on doit avoir en Jésus-Christ.He  was the first to suspect that Perrault's tales were not written by Charles Perrault's son, as announced by the publishers, but by the academician himself - or at least at second hand. De Villiers joined the Jesuits on 6 June 1666 and distinguished himself in the careers of teaching and preaching. He took the order of priesthood and exercised the holy ministry. In 1689 he left the Jesuits to join the unreformed Cluny order. A writer and essayist, he composed or printed most of the works that came from his pen. Boileau mentions the Abbé de Villiers in his poetry, and calls him "the Matamore of Cluny", "because he had a bold air and imperious speech". He never put his name to his works.

=500  \\$aLe Misant(h)rope was a Dutch journal originally published every monday from May 19th 1711 tot December 26th 1712 . Published in 2 vols. in The Hague by T.Johnson in 1711 and 1712. The magazine was reprinted in 1726 (own revision by Van Effen) in The Hague; 1741 (Lausanne/Geneva) and twice in 1742 (Amsterdam and The Hague).
=500  \\$aJustus van Effen was a Dutch author, who wrote chiefly in French but also made crucial contributions to Dutch literature. A journalist, he imitated The Spectator with the publication of the Dutch-language Hollandsche Spectator. He gained international fame as a writer of French periodicals and a translator from English into French, and he is also recognized as one of the most important Dutch language writers of the 18th century and an influential figure of the Dutch Enlightenment
=500  \\$aOften considered as one of the best essayistic texts from the early Enlightenment.
=500  \\$aFrontispiece vol.1 is an engraved portrait of the author by Pieter Tanjé (1706-1761)  after des Angeles (1716-1761)

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aEffen, Justus van$d1684-1735$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2574405$98518
=245  \\$aLa Bagatelle, $bou Discours ironiques$n1-2/2
=250  \\$arev. ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bUytwerf$c1742
=300  \\$a2 vols ([xxvi]-300-[8] + 289-[9] pages)$btitle pages in red and black ink
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=490  \\$aOeuvres diverses de Mr. Juste van Effen$v3-4/4
=500  \\$aMoral observations in a satirical tone. Interests: fashion, religion, morals. Authors studied: Addison, Swift, La Bruyère.
=500  \\$aDutch Journal published every thursday and monday between 5 mai 1718 and 13 avril 1719. 
=500  \\$aAlready the author of several journals including the first spectator in French (Le Misanthrope), Justus van Effen attempted to capture the Regency spirit in France with La Bagatelle. Produced as a twice-weekly quarter sheet, La Bagatelle included witty observations on contemporary society, literary controversies, bolder, more subversive reflections on questions of religion, as well as short works of poetry and prose. 
=500  \\$aSince 1718, the publication of the Literary Journal had been delayed by the nonchalance of the bookseller Johnson. For van Effen this meant a considerable loss of money, so he sought some compensation. He launched La Bagatelle for personal reasons.
=500  \\$aThe author intended (cf. Preface) to lead men from the ridiculousness of custom and fashion to Reason; but his ironic style was not understood. Convinced of his error, he wanted to change his plan: "I will put a capital I on the frontispiece of my Feuille Volante, so that the public will be aware of it" (I, as in Irony), he declares at the end of the first volume. In fact, van Effen himself, a serious man, found it difficult to sustain the satirical tone. In short, La Bagatelle was not a success.
=500  \\$aPreface in the issue of Monday 5 September 1718: "to bring Men back from the ridiculous impressions of Custom and Fashion to the eternal and invariable principles of Reason, which must be the only Rule of our Conduct".
=504  \\$aevery volume contains an index
=504  \\$aEdited by James L. Schorr (ed.), ‘La Bagatelle’ (1718-1719): a critical edition of Justus van Effen’s journal, in  'Oxford University Studies in the Enlightenment', November 2014. ISBN 9780729411493, 352 pages,
=590  \\$aOù l'on prête des Sophismes ingénieux au Vice & à l'Extravagance, pour en faire mieux sentir le ridicule. Par Mr. van Effen, Docteur en Droit, & Membre de la Société Royale de Londres

=100  \\$aDrouaux, Étienne$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q28494512$98519
=245  \\$aMéthode nouvelle pour apprendre le plain-chant$bDivise en quatre parties

=300  \\$a[viii]-144 pages$bmusical examples
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aOriginally published in 1672 Paris by Robert & Ballard
=500  \\$aÉtienne Drouaux was a musician and composer active in Paris in the last third of the 17th century.
=500  \\$aDrouaux is best known as the author of a method of plainsong which enjoyed a certain success, since about ten editions were published between 1672 and 1705. This method was part of a wave of publications of new methods which tended to give a somewhat secure basis to the practice of plainchant. But it appears that Drouaux was largely inspired by Jean Millet's method of 1666, keeping the most practical elements and eliminating the old authorities that encumbered it.
=500  \\$aDrouaux' first name is really Étienne (or Estienne), not Henri Blaise, as Fétis or Ton thought

=100  \\$aMaffei, Scipione$d1675-1755$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1587432$96886
=245  \\$aDe gli anfiteatri e singolarmente del Veronese $blibri due
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aVerona$bTumermani$c1728
=300  \\$a[12]-348-[12] pages, 14 inserted folded pages with plates$bbound in white vellum, illustrations, engraved title page
=500  \\$aMaffei was a Venetian writer and art critic, author of many articles and plays. An antiquarian with a humanist education whose publications on Etruscan antiquities stand as incunables of Etruscology. Founder of the Lapidary Museum of Verona. A multifaceted figure in the Italian and European panorama. Military, philosopher, poet, playwright, historian, scientist, opera librettist, but above all a passionate fanatic of antiquities. He was an avid collector of ancient manuscripts and epigraphs, which he acquired in Verona, Italy or brought from all over the Mediterranean basin thanks to the possessions of the Republic of Venice, of which Verona was a part. Maffei was a prominent member of the Veronese Accademia Filarmonica and he worked for the realization of the theater that would be inaugurated in 1732 with Vivaldi's 'La fida ninfa', for which he wrote the libretto.

=041  \\$alat
=100  \\$aMaggi, Girolamo$dc. 1523-1572$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q5564769$98540
=245  \\$aDe equuleo
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bFrisius$c1664
=300  \\$a[xxx]-196-[14] pages$bbound in white vellum, engraved title page, illustrations, 1 inserted folded page$c7x13 cm
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aTreatise on torture devices written in 1571, first published posthumously 1609.
=500  \\$aMaggi was an Italian scholar, jurist, poet, military engineer, urban planner, philologist, archaeologist, mathematician, and naturalist who studied at Bologna under Francis Robortello. He authored several works, including a collection of poems on the Flemish wars, and several on the subject of philosophy.
=500  \\$aMaggi was a judge and military defense engineer in Famagusta on Cyprus when the island was invaded by Ottoman Turks in 1571. Besieged by the Turks, he invented machines to defend Famagusta against their attacks. When the island was conquered, Maggi was sent to the dungeons at Constantinople where, locked in chains, he wrote from memory two detailed treatises, De tintinnabulis, on bells and carillons, and the explicitly illustrated De equuleo, on torture devices.In attempts to be freed, he dedicated the first treatise to Carolus Rym (Charles Ramire), ambassador to the Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian II, and the second treatise to François de Noailles, bishop of Aire and ambassador to the King of France. They were pleased with his works, and endeavoured to obtain his release. Their efforts, however, were brought to light as he was being released to the Italian ambassador. The prison captain ordered him to be detained and executed by strangulation. His two treatises were published posthumously in 1608 and 1609, respectively.

=500  \\$aMaggi was an Italian scholar, jurist, poet, military engineer, urban planner, philologist, archaeologist, mathematician, and naturalist who studied at Bologna under Francis Robortello. He authored several works, including a collection of poems on the Flemish wars, and several on the subject of philosophy.

=500  \\$aMaggi was a judge and military defense engineer in Famagusta on Cyprus when the island was invaded by Ottoman Turks in 1571. Besieged by the Turks, he invented machines to defend Famagusta against their attacks. When the island was conquered, Maggi was sent to the dungeons at Constantinople where, locked in chains, he wrote from memory two detailed treatises, De tintinnabulis, on bells and carillons, and the explicitly illustrated De equuleo, on torture devices.In attempts to be freed, he dedicated the first treatise to Carolus Rym (Charles Ramire), ambassador to the Holy Roman Emperor Maximilian II, and the second treatise to François de Noailles, bishop of Aire and ambassador to the King of France. The prison captain ordered him to be detained and executed by strangulation. His two treatises were published posthumously in 1608 and 1609, respectively.

=041  \\$afre
=100  \\$aTiton du Tillet, Évrard$d1677-1762$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q3592904$97631
=245  \\$aDescription du Parnasse François, exécuté en bronze
=260  \\$aParis$bCoignard$c1727
=300  \\$axxviii-366-[10] pages
=500  \\$abiographical chronicle, composed of brief anecdotal vite of famous French poets and musicians of his time, under the reign of Louis XIV and the Régence
=500  \\$aTiton du Tillet had the privilege of receiving the celebrities of his time, and from 1708 he was at work on an imposing project: to create a garden surrounding a monument, "the French Parnassus" (Le Parnasse françois), celebrating the glory of French poets and musicians under the reign of Louis XIV. The monument was to represent Mount Parnassus, ornamented with laurels and myrtle, with Louis XIV in the figure of Apollo at the summit, playing the lyre. The expected expenditure, estimated at nearly two million livres, forced him to terminate the project. He then decided to carry the project out to some extent in a virtual form: he published in 1727, "a Description of the Parnasse François" followed by "an alphabetical List of the Poets and Musicians gathered on this monument". In 1732, he published a second edition and increased the notes on the lives of the poets and musicians. Two further supplements were published in 1743 and 1755. This collection constitutes an invaluable source of biographical information for the mysterious Monsieur de Sainte-Colombe, Marin Marais, Louis Couperin, Michel Richard Delalande, Nicolas Bernier and other celebrated poets and musicians.

=041  \\$ager$hdan
=100  \\$aHolberg, Ludvig$d1684-1754$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q216692$98546
=245  \\$aPeter Paars$bein comisches Heldengedicht
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLeipzig$bMumme$c1750
=300  \\$a[lxviii]-420 pages$b14 inserted engraved plates, engraved title pages and frontispiece
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aTitle page has emblem "In Spe et Labore"
=500  \\$aPeder Paars is a comic-epic poem that appeared in four parts in the years 1719-20 under the pseudonym of Hans Michelsen. The poem is a parody of the heroic epics of antiquity and Renaissance. Holberg particularly alludes to Vergil's great Roman epic Aeneid.
=500  \\$aThe poem enjoyed great success, but the description of conditions on Anholt prompted the then owner, Frederik Rostgaard, to complain to the king, demanding that the book be burned by the executioner. The king nevertheless decided that the writing - although it "could rather have been omitted than written" - could be accepted, as it was a "fictitious sketch." 
=500  \\$aHolberg was a writer, essayist, philosopher, historian and playwright born in Bergen, Norway, during the time of the Dano-Norwegian dual monarchy. He was influenced by Humanism, the Enlightenment and the Baroque. Holberg is considered the founder of modern Danish and Norwegian literature. He is best known for the comedies he wrote in 1722–1723 for the Lille Grønnegade Theatre in Copenhagen.
=500  \\$aPaars was a breakthrough in Holberg's writing in the direction of satire and the many comedies for which he is still known.
=500  \\$aThe composer J.A. Scheibe translated Peder Paars into German. In 1740 he became kapellmeister at the court of the danisch king Christian IV, and remained in Denmark until his death. He had a very sharp pen, evident in his satirical writings or political pamphlets,  but also in the first biography of his friend Baron Ludvig Holberg, The biography not only provides information on Holberg but also indirectly on Scheibe.
=504  \\$aPaars and his crew discover that the inhabitants of Anholt, who "live Christianly and feed on debris", are plundering and robbing the castaways. The rest of the island is watching the commoners who live in the blackest superstition. The bailiff passes judgement in his own favour, while the priest relies on old Catholic sermons. 
=504  \\$ahttps://dansklitteraturshistorie.lex.dk/Det_komiske_helteepos_Peder_Paars

https://www.hf.uio.no/imv/english/research/projects/power/projectdescription/holberg/

=500  \\$aJoseph Addison was an English essayist, poet, playwright and politician. His name is usually remembered alongside that of his long-standing friend Richard Steele, with whom he founded The Spectator magazine. His simple prose style marked the end of the mannerisms and conventional classical images of the 17th century.[
=500  \\$aThe Gallica-digitalisation in the version revised by the actor Jean Claude Gilles Colson (1725-1778) dit Bellecour, was according to Léris first performed in 1762:
https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k9738993k.texteImage
=500  \\$a First edition of the French translation by Destouches. 
=520  \\$aLady Truman is apparently widowed when she receives word that her husband Sir George has been killed in battle during the recent war. As she is now the wealthy owner of an estate she is pursued by two suitors, but concerningly the house is disturbed at night by repeated sounds of ghostly drumming. After the drumming has scared off the two suitors Mr. Tinsel and Mr. Fantome it is revealed to be the work of Sir George, still very much alive.

=500  \\$aJohann Joseph Kausch was a Silesian physician and writer. He not only wrote various writings and treatises in the field of medicine, but also published writings on aesthetics, poetry and politics. In Trachenberg, as personal physician at the court of Prince Franz Philipp Adrian Hatzfeld (1717-1779), he began to study psychology through the study of French philosophers.

=041  \\$alat$hlat
=245  \\$aMonita secreta of de geheime instructiën die door de Jesuieten in stilte worden nageleefd
=260  \\$aOostburg$bBronswijk$c1868
=300  \\$a56 pages
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aAnti-Jesuit pamphlet
=500  \\$aThe Monita secreta ("Secret Instructions") is an anonymous document from 1614 whose original title is Monita privata Societatis Iesu . This booklet gives instructions to the Jesuits on how to proceed in order to gain power and wealth. It is a fake - and known as such since 1615 - but it had great success with the enemies of the Jesuits, including the 19th and 20th centuries.  Scholars regard the document as an anti-Jesuit forgery, written by Hieronymus Zahorowski, a Jesuit dismissed from the Order.
=520  \\$aAccording to the Monita, Jesuits are to use every means at their disposal to acquire wealth for the order. For instance, Jesuits are encouraged to entice promising young men to enter the order and endow it with their estates; rich widows are to be cajoled and dissuaded from remarriage. Every means is to be used for the advancement of Jesuits to bishoprics or other ecclesiastical dignities and to discredit the members of other orders, while the world is to be persuaded that the Society is animated by the purest and least interested motives: the reputation of those who quit it is to be assailed and maligned in every way.
